Once upon a time, there was a little bird named Flappy. Flappy was a very special bird, because he had a very special tail. His tail was made of colourful feathers and it always waved in the wind.

One day Flappy and his friends had a picnic at the park. Flappy was so excited! He flew around and played while the others were eating their lunch.

Suddenly, Flappy saw something interesting! He flew down to take a closer look. It was a pot full of beautiful feathers! Flappy kept looking and saw something else. It was a big spoon!

Flappy hopped closer and saw that the spoon was stirring the feathers inside the pot. He watched for a few moments and then he had an exciting idea. Flappy flew into the pot, grabbed a feather and hopped out. He waved it in the wind and it made a cool sound.

Flappy and his friends had a lot of fun with the feather. It was very interesting! They spent the rest of the day playing and stirring the feathers in the pot.

Jake was very adventurous. He saw an exit and he wanted to explore it. He asked his mom if he could go and she said it was okay.

Jake excitedly went to the exit. He collected some sticks and leaves. He also found a beautiful butterfly.

He put all of his collections into his pocket and went back to his mom. She was so happy to see all of his collections.

Jake had such a great time. He was so happy to be able to explore and collect things. He couldn't wait for his next adventurous day!

Anna and Ben are friends. They like to play catch with a ball. They throw the ball to each other and catch it with their hands. Sometimes they miss and the ball falls on the ground. Then they run to get it and start again.

One day, they play catch in the park. There are many people and animals in the park. Anna throws the ball to Ben, but Ben does not catch it. The ball flies over his head and lands near a stand. The stand has many flowers and pots. A lady is selling the flowers and pots. She is not happy to see the ball near her stand.

She picks up the ball and shouts at Anna and Ben. She says they are bad and careless. She says they could break her flowers and pots. She says she will not give them back the ball. She puts the ball in a big pot and turns away.

Anna and Ben are sad and scared. They want their ball back. They say they are sorry and they did not mean to hurt the lady or her stand. They ask her to be kind and compassionate. They say they will be more careful next time.

The lady hears them and looks at them. She sees their tears and their sorry faces. She feels sorry for them too. She remembers that she was once a child who liked to play catch. She decides to be compassionate and give them back the ball. She takes the ball out of the pot and hands it to Anna and Ben. She tells them to be more careful and to have fun. She smiles and they smile too.

Anna and Ben thank the lady and hug her. They take their ball and run to a different place in the park. They play catch again, but they watch out for people and animals and stands. They are happy and grateful. They are friends.

Today was a fun day. Momma and Daddy took Sam to the park. Sam ran around and fit all the way there. He fit on the swings and the slides too.

When Sam got hungry, Momma gave him a tasty snack. He loved the apples. They were so sweet and juicy.

Next, they fit in a big sandbox. Sam filled up a bucket with sand and then carried it around. He made towers and filled up big trucks.

After the park, they went back home. Sam was so tired. He ate dinner and it was the best food ever. It was so yummy and tasty.

Today was a fun day and Sam fit in a lot of fun activities.

Once upon a time, there was a helpful little girl. She wanted to do something nice for her family, so she decided to make muffins. She gathered all the ingredients, read the recipe and got to work.

She performed each step carefully, adding flour, milk and eggs together until she had a smooth batter. She poured the batter into muffin pans and put them into the oven.

The muffins baked in the oven, making the house smell really good. Finally, the timer dinged and the muffins were ready. She carefully took them out of the oven, and they smelled delicious!

The little girl was so pleased with her muffins that she shared them with her family. Everyone was so happy and grateful for her helpful work. The muffins were a delicious treat, and it was a wonderful family moment!

Lila and Ben were playing outside with their toys. They liked to make roads and bridges with the sand and the stones. They had a lot of fun together.

But then, the sky became dark and grey. They heard a loud noise. It was thunder. They saw a bright light. It was lightning. They felt something wet on their faces. It was rain.

"Let's go inside, Lila!" Ben said. "The rain is too much. It can hurt us."

"No, Ben!" Lila said. "The rain is fine. It is just water. It is not bad. It is a gift from the spirit."

"What spirit?" Ben asked.

"The spirit of the sky. He makes the rain and the thunder and the lightning. He is very powerful and kind. He gives us water to drink and to grow. He cleans the air and the earth. He makes the flowers and the grass and the trees happy. He is our friend." Lila said.

Ben looked at Lila. He was not sure. He was scared of the noise and the light. He wanted to go inside and be safe and warm.

But he also saw that Lila was not scared. She was smiling and laughing. She opened her arms and spun around. She caught the raindrops with her tongue. She looked happy and free.

Ben thought for a moment. He decided to try. He opened his arms and spun around. He caught the raindrops with his tongue. He felt the water on his skin and hair. He felt a tickle in his belly. He started to smile and laugh.

He looked at Lila. She looked at him. They both giggled. They felt the spirit of the sky in their hearts. They felt fine.

Once upon a time, there was a little girl named Anna. She was very brave and always wanted to explore. One day, she decided to take a walk in the forest.

As Anna was walking, she saw a big tree and started to walk towards it. Suddenly, she felt something slippery under her feet, and she slipped and fell on the ground.

Anna was very upset and she started to cry. She was scared and thought she would never be able to get back home. But then something magical happened.

A small group of friendly forest animals came to help her. They helped Anna to get back up and took her back home.

From then on, Anna always made sure to be careful when walking in the forest.

The End.

Once upon a time, there was a little girl named Lily. She loved to play outside and catch butterflies. One day, she saw a farmer harvesting wheat in the field. She asked the farmer what he was doing, and he explained that he was collecting the wheat to make bread.

Lily thought it would be fun to catch some wheat too. She tried to grab a handful, but it was too hard and inflexible. The farmer showed her how to gently hold the wheat and flex it to make it easier to catch.

Lily learned that being gentle and flexible can help you catch things better. She also learned that wheat is an important ingredient in making bread, which is a delicious and nutritious food. From that day on, Lily made sure to be gentle and flexible in everything she did, and she always appreciated the value of wheat.

One of the friends said, "I want to play more. Can we play one more time?"

The other friends said, "No, it's too dark and we need to go home. We can play again tomorrow."

The friend who wanted to play more felt sad, but knew it was time to end the game. They all said goodbye and went home. The end.

Lily and Max were going on a safari with their mom and dad. They were very excited to see the animals. They packed their hats, water, and snacks in a big bag.

On the way to the safari park, Max was grumpy. He did not want to share his snacks with Lily. He said, "These are mine! Go away!" Lily was sad. She wanted to have some snacks too. She said, "That's not nice, Max. We are supposed to share."

Mom and dad heard them fighting. They said, "Stop it, both of you. We are almost there. You can have your snacks later. Now, look out the window and see the animals."

Lily and Max looked out the window. They saw zebras, giraffes, elephants, and lions. They forgot about their snacks. They said, "Wow! Look at them! They are so big and beautiful!"

They got to the safari park. They got out of the car and followed a guide. The guide showed them more animals and told them stories. Lily and Max listened and asked questions. They learned a lot.

At the end of the safari, they went back to the car. They were hungry and thirsty. They remembered their snacks. They looked at each other and smiled. They said, "Sorry, we were grumpy. Do you want to share?" They nodded and hugged. They opened their bag and shared their snacks. They were happy. They had a fun day.

The man smiled and said, "I can help you get to the barn. It's not too far away, let's go!" The little girl was so relieved and followed the man to the barn. When they arrived, everyone clapped to welcome her. She was so happy and no longer felt embarrassed.

Once upon a time, there was a little boy named Timmy. He loved to ride his bike in the park. One day, he saw his friend Billy and they decided to ride together. They rode and rode until they saw a big tree. Timmy wanted to look up at the tree, but he couldn't see the top.

Suddenly, Timmy fell off his bike and hurt his knee. He was upset and started to cry. Billy asked him, "Are you okay?" Timmy shook his head and said, "No, it hurts." Billy helped him up and they walked to a nearby bench. Timmy's mom came over and gave him a band-aid. He felt much better and they all laughed and played together. The end.

One day, a little girl named Lucy was playing in her backyard. She was having lots of fun in the dirt. Lucy saw a bug, so she bent down and picked up some soil. She threw it in the air and then she kicked it. It flew really high! She laughed and laughed.

The noise was very loud, and her mom came to the door to see what was going on. She saw Lucy kicking the soil and said, "No, Lucy! Don't kick the soil!"

Lucy stopped. She looked at the soil and then at her mom. She said "OK" and put the soil back on the ground. She promised her mom that she would not kick it again.

Then, she started playing with some toys. She was having lots of fun! Lucy forgot all about the soil, but she always remembered to be careful with it - and not to kick it again.

Once upon a time there was a small boy called Peter. Peter loved to eat squash. He went to his garden to pick the best squashes. He found a big, dry squash so he decided to take it home for lunch.

Peter took the squash to the kitchen and washed it carefully. Then he cut it into small pieces with a knife. He put all the pieces into a pan and added some salt and pepper.

Next he put the pan on the stove and cooked the squash until it was soft. He stirred it again and again until everything tasted delicious.

At last he took the pan out of the stove and ate his squash. He loved it! Every bite tasted like sunshine.

The End

Once upon a time, there was a little girl named Sarah. Sarah was three-years-old and very curious. She loved to explore the world around her.

One day, she went out for a walk with her mommy. They went through a field of tall grass and saw a beautiful landscape. Sarah fell in love with it and looked at it with an adorable expression.

Sarah turned to her mommy and said, "Mommy, why do we not have a landscape like this at home?"

Her mommy smiled and said, "We can get one, Sarah, but we need to study a little bit first. We need to know how to take care of it before we can have one of our own."

Sarah was excited and started to study the landscape some more. Every day she went out with her mommy and learned something new. After some time, they were ready to have a landscape of their own at home.

When they got home, Sarah was thrilled to see the beautiful and adorable landscape they had created. She ran around it, playing and laughing.

And they all lived happily ever after.

One day, Lily and her parents were walking in the park. Suddenly, she saw a bright red automobile by the lake. She was so happy and excited that she started running towards it.

"Don't act silly, Lily," said her Dad.

But she didn't listen and kept running towards the car. When she reached it, she was surprised to see a man sitting in the driver's seat. Suddenly, that man started and drove away quickly.

Lily was very scared, but her Dad was there to help her. He hugged her tight and reassured her that everything was okay. He told her she always has to be careful and think before acting.

Lily felt better hearing her Dad's words. Even though the car was gone, she was still happy because she was safe with her Dad. She hugged him and they started walking back home, feeling happy together.

Molly then noticed and said, "Don't worry Lucy, I have a match for your teddy bear!"

Lucy was delighted and replied, "Really? Where is it?"

Molly smiled and said, "I knew it would be a perfect match when I saw it. Come with me and I'll show you."

So, the two friends went off together, hand in hand, and after a short walk in the park, they reached a special shop. Inside, there was an amazing selection of toys and Lucy could hardly contain her excitement.

Once upon a time, there was a little bird named Max. One day, Max saw a broken cloud in the sky. He wanted to have it, but he could not reach it. So he hopped and he flapped his wings until he was floating high up in the sky. Max was so happy! He laughed and clapped his hands.

Max flew closer and closer to the broken cloud. When he was right in front of it, he jumped right in. He was lost in the broken cloud. It was so big and fluffy. Max looked around him and enjoyed the clouds.

But then something happened. Suddenly the wind blew and the broken cloud was no longer broken. It was together again. Max looked all around him, and he was happy. He had his own cloud! He sang and danced and he was so excited.

And then Max flew away, and he never forgot his broken cloud.

His mom tried to convince him by showing him his favorite toy on display in the bathroom, but Timmy still didn't want to take a bath. Finally, his mom had an idea. After the bath, Timmy's hair was clean and shiny. He was happy that he took a bath and he even thanked his mom for making it fun. From that day on, Timmy didn't mind taking baths anymore.

Once upon a time there was a wise owl who loved to carry spaghetti. Every day, he gathered as much spaghetti as he could carry and flew away. As he flew, he would drop some of the spaghetti in different places. He wanted to share it with everyone!

Once upon a time, there was a fat princess. She lived in a tall castle, with high walls around it. Every day, she would look out of her window and admire her kingdom.

But one day, the princess noticed something strange. All the trees and animals were walking backwards! Even the waves on the lake reversed themselves. She was so surprised and she wanted to know what had happened.

The princess asked the gardener, but he had no idea. Then she asked the cook, but he too was baffled. In the end, the princess decided to find out the mystery herself.

So the princess grabbed her long cloak and stepped out of her castle. She walked around her kingdom but couldn't find an answer. Suddenly, she saw a wise old owl perched on a nearby tree.

"Oh, wise owl," the princess said. "Why is everything walking backwards?"

The wise owl smiled and said, "My dear princess, you have used the magical power of reverse. Everything knows the princess' royal command and will always obey it!"

The princess was so happy! From that day on, she used the magical power of reverse as she liked. She even used it to make her kingdom more beautiful than ever before.

The end.

It was a bright and sunny day. Johnny was out with his dad and they had come to the swamp. Dad wanted to show Johnny the animals and plants that lived in the swamp. Johnny was excited but also a bit scared.

Dad took Johnny to the edge of the swamp, where the water was still and calm. But soon the calm water started to get rougher, and dad said to be careful. Dad pointed out all the different animals and explained why they chose to live in the swamp.

Suddenly, dad stopped and said it was time to raise their voices and make some noise. Johnny was confused, but then he heard something: a loud splash coming from the swamp! Dad had warned him it was mating season, and sure enough there were two big alligators raising a little baby!

Johnny couldn't believe his eyes and he was so excited. Dad looked proud, and told Johnny that it was ok to be scared sometimes, but it was also ok to be curious and learn about nature. Johnny nodded and said that he wanted to come back to the swamp soon.

They all had so much fun. After a while, the sun went down and the otter swam back home. He had had a really amazing day!

When he touched the icy crystal he heard a sound. Someone was talking! It said "Touch me and I will be your friend.

Sam was scared, but he wanted to make a new friend. He put his nose closer and he said "Hello?

Then, a very friendly voice answered "Hello, Sam! I am the icy crystal. I can help you find the lost numbers in your skin. Would you like that?

Ben and Mia liked to play with magnets. They had many magnets of different shapes and colors. They liked to stick them on the fridge, on the door, on the table. They liked to see how the magnets pulled or pushed each other.

One day, they found a new magnet in their toy box. It was a ring magnet. It was shiny and silver. It looked very modern. Ben and Mia wondered what it could do.

"Let's try it on the fridge," Ben said.

"OK," Mia agreed.

They ran to the kitchen and put the ring magnet on the fridge. It stuck very well. They tried to pull it off, but it was hard.

"Wow, this is a strong magnet," Ben said.

"Maybe it can stick to other things too," Mia said.

They looked around the room and saw a phone on the counter. It was their mom's phone. It was also shiny and silver. It looked very modern too.

"Let's try it on the phone," Mia said.

"OK," Ben agreed.

They took the ring magnet and put it on the phone. It stuck very well too. They tried to pull it off, but it was harder.

"Wow, this is a very strong magnet," Mia said.

But then, something strange happened. The phone started to make a loud noise. It was ringing. Ben and Mia were scared. They did not know what to do.

"Mom, mom, help!" they shouted.

Their mom came running from the living room. She saw the phone and the magnet. She looked angry.

"Ben, Mia, what have you done?" she asked.

She took the phone and the magnet. She tried to separate them, but it was very hard. She had to use a lot of force. She finally managed to pull them apart.

She looked at the phone and saw that it was broken. The screen was cracked. The buttons were stuck. The sound was distorted.

She looked at Ben and Mia and said, "This was a very bad idea. You should never put magnets on phones. Magnets can damage phones. Phones are not toys. They are important and expensive. You have to be careful and respectful with them. Do you understand?"

Ben and Mia nodded. They felt sorry and ashamed. They did not mean to break the phone. They did not know that magnets could hurt phones. They just wanted to play and have fun.

They said, "We are sorry, mom. We did not know. We will not do it again. We love you."

Their mom sighed. She was still angry, but she also loved them. She said, "I love you too. But you have to be more responsible and sensible. You have to learn from your mistakes. And you have to help me fix the phone. Come on, let's go to the store and see what we can do."

Suddenly, he heard a loud noise again. This time it was a loud bang and Dave stopped running. He looked around and saw his Dad shooting. His Dad had a gun and he was shooting insects with it. Dave watched as the insects fell from the sky.

He felt scared and he wanted to go to his Dad, but he was too scared to move. His Dad finished shooting and smiled at Dave. He said, "It's okay. You can come here. I won't shoot any more insects."

Dave felt relieved and he ran to his Dad. Together they watched the insects fly away and Dave was happy that the loud noises were gone.

Once upon a time there was a little girl named Millie. She had long brown hair and liked to rub it when she was feeling sleepy. Millie had a big friend named Bob.

One day they decided to go to the park. Millie was so excited to go and asked her friend to count with her.

Bob said, "1,2,3,4,5,6,7, let's go!"

Millie rubbed her hair and said, "Yes, let's go!"

Once they arrived at the park, Millie and Bob counted all of the trees. They counted and counted until they were very sleepy.

Millie said, "Let's go home now and take a nap. We can count again tomorrow!"

Bob nodded his head and said, "Yes, let's go home."

So Millie and Bob went home and quickly fell asleep. They dreamed of counting things all night long. The end!

Anna and Ben are playing hide and seek in the kitchen. Anna is the seeker and Ben is the hider. Ben looks for a good place to hide. He sees the fridge and opens it. He sees a big bottle of milk and thinks it is a good hiding spot. He climbs into the fridge and closes the door behind him. He hopes Anna will not find him.

Anna counts to ten and then says, "Ready or not, here I come!" She looks around the kitchen and tries to find Ben. She does not see him under the table, behind the curtains, or in the cabinets. She wonders where he is. She hears a small noise from the fridge. She walks to the fridge and opens it. She sees Ben sitting in the fridge, holding the bottle of milk. She laughs and says, "I found you, Ben! You are hiding in the fridge with the milk!"

Ben feels embarrassed. He did not think Anna would find him so easily. He also feels cold and wet. The milk has spilled on his clothes and hair. He says, "I'm sorry, Anna. I thought it was a good hiding spot. But it was not. It was a bad hiding spot. And now I'm cold and wet and sticky."

Anna says, "It's okay, Ben. Don't be embarrassed. It was a funny hiding spot. But not a smart one. Come on, let's get you out of the fridge and clean you up. And then we can play another game. Maybe you can be the seeker and I can be the hider. And I will not hide in the fridge with the milk."

"Well Millie," said her dad, "a teaspoon is a small spoon that we use to scoop up things and measure ingredients when we are cooking."

Millie was so curious that she decided to go on an adventure around the farm. She was looking for a teaspoon. She guessed that there were many hiding on the farm somewhere.

So Millie roamed around all day, searching for a teaspoon. The farm was so big and Millie searched in all the different places, but she couldn't find any teaspoon.

Finally, at the end of the day, Millie stopped and sat down outside a old, rich house. As she was sitting there, she spotted a large silver teaspoon on a table in the house.

Millie jumped up with joy and ran over to the house. She reached out to grab the teaspoon but a woman came out of the house and said, "What are you doing here little girl?"

Millie told the woman why she was there and the woman smiled kindly and said, "I am happy to give this teaspoon to you. It was given to me by my grandmother and I think it would be nice for you to have it

Once upon a time, there was a little bunny named Benny. Benny loved to play outside in the forest, but he was always scared of the big animals that lived there. One day, Benny found a magazine that had a picture of a strong and brave bear on it. Benny wanted to be like the bear and protect himself from the scary animals.

Benny asked his mommy to help him make a tight cape just like the bear's. His mommy made it for him and Benny felt very brave wearing it. When he went outside to play, he saw a big wolf coming towards him. Benny remembered what he learned from the magazine and put on his cape, feeling very strong.

The wolf tried to scare Benny, but Benny stood tall and protected himself with his cape. The wolf ran away and Benny felt very proud of himself. From that day on, Benny knew that he didn't have to be scared anymore. He had his tight cape to protect him and he felt very brave. The moral of the story is that we can protect ourselves by being brave and using the things we have.

Tuesday was a sunny day. Mum and Dad took Alex outside to go for a walk in the park. Alex saw lots of birds and he wanted to feed them some bread. Dad said, "Let's make a humble request to the birds," and he put his hands together and bowed his head. Alex did the same.

Dad said, "Please birds, would you like some bread?" One of the birds flew close to them and and accepted the request! Alex was excited and said, "Me too, me too!"

Dad gave some bread to the bird and then he shared some with Alex. Alex had so much fun feeding the birds that he asked to do it on Tuesdays from then on.

The family smiled. "That's a lovely request, Alex," said Mum. They agreed to go to the park every Tuesday to feed the birds.

Once upon a time there was a little girl who wanted to go and play outside. She looked out the window, but the sky seemed very gloomy. She begun to get a bit sad, so she decided to peek around and search for something fun to do. Then she saw it! It was a big mug on the floor!

Once upon a time there was a little girl named Jane. She loved to play in the backyard with her friends. One day, she and her friends wanted to have a conversation. Jane could hear everyone perfectly, but her best friend Sarah could not. Sarah was deaf.

Jane wanted to help her friend. She realized that mail was a way for people to communicate without having to hear or talk. So she wrote a letter to Sarah and sent it off in the mail.

When Sarah received the letter, she was so excited! She couldn't believe Jane had thought of it. She wrote back and sent it back in the mail.

Back and forth they wrote letters. Jane and Sarah could now talk even though they lived far apart. They realized they could write letters to each other every day!

Since then, Jane and Sarah have been the best of friends. They wrote letters to each other all the time, even when they lived far away. They were so happy that they figured out how to communicate without hearing or talking.

Sara and Tom were friends who liked to play with their toys. One day, they found a whip in the garage. It was long and black and had a handle. Sara thought it was pretty and wanted to try it.

"Can I have the whip, Tom?" Sara asked.

"No, it's mine. I found it first," Tom said.

"Please, Tom. Just for a little bit. I'll give it back to you," Sara begged.

"Fine, but only for a minute. Don't delay, or I'll be angry," Tom said.

Sara took the whip and ran outside. She swung it in the air and made a loud noise. She felt powerful and happy. She forgot about Tom and his warning.

Tom waited and waited for Sara to come back. He got bored and angry. He decided to go outside and get his whip back. He saw Sara playing with the whip and not paying attention to him.

"Hey, Sara! Give me back my whip! You delayed too long!" Tom shouted.

Sara turned around and saw Tom. She was scared and sorry. She tried to give him back the whip, but it was too late. Tom was so mad that he grabbed the whip and hit Sara with it. Sara cried out in pain and dropped the whip. She had a red mark on her arm where the whip hit her.

Tom felt bad and sorry. He didn't mean to hurt Sara. He just wanted his whip back. He picked up the whip and ran back to the garage. He hid the whip and hoped no one would find it.

Sara ran back to her house. She had tears in her eyes and blood on her arm. She told her mom what happened. Her mom was angry and sad. She called Tom's mom and told her what happened. Tom's mom was angry and sad too. She scolded Tom and took away his toys. She made him apologize to Sara and say sorry.

Sara and Tom were not friends anymore. They learned a hard lesson. They learned that whips are not toys. They learned that sharing is better than fighting. They learned that delaying can cause trouble. They learned that pretty things can be dangerous.

"Where will the lizard sleep?" dad asks.

"The lizard will sleep in a big tank with rocks and water and plants," Anna says. "I can put it in my room or in the living room."

"How will you keep the lizard safe and happy?" mom and dad ask.

"I will keep the lizard safe and happy by giving it a name and a toy and a friend," Anna says. "I will talk to it and pet it and watch it."

"Mom, can we have some cookies?" Tom asked.

"Not now, boys. It's almost time for lunch. You can have one cookie each after you finish your food," Mom said.

Tom and Sam were not happy. They wanted the cookies now. They decided to sneak some when Mom was not looking. They opened the jar and took out two cookies each. They ate them quickly and put the jar back in the cabinet.

But they did not close the cabinet door properly. It was still a little bit open. Tom saw it and tried to push it with his hand. But it did not close. He got angry and kicked the cabinet door hard.

Bang! The cabinet door slammed shut, but the jar of cookies fell down and broke. Cookies and glass pieces were everywhere on the floor. Mom heard the noise and came to the kitchen.

"What happened here?" Mom asked.

Tom and Sam were scared. They knew they did something bad. They did not say anything.

"Did you boys take the cookies without asking me?" Mom asked.

Tom and Sam nodded. They felt sorry.

"And did you kick the cabinet door and break the jar?" Mom asked.

Tom nodded. He felt more sorry.

Mom was not happy. She was angry and sad. She told Tom and Sam to go to their room and think about what they did. She also told them they could not have any more cookies for a week. She said they had to learn to listen to her and to be careful with things.

Tom and Sam went to their room. They did not want to play. They wanted to hug Mom and say they were sorry. They learned that kicking things and taking things without asking were not good. They learned that they had to be fine boys who respected Mom and the kitchen.

From then on, Bob never flew too close to the cliff again. He had learned his lesson, and never wanted to pass the cliff again!

The children had all brought with them a snack to eat between their playing. The snacks were all shapes and sizes and the mouse thought they looked delicious. He wanted to fit in with the children, so he grabbed one of the snacks off the ground and ran away with it.

The other children weren't eating their snacks; they were sharing them with each other, laughing and talking happily. Lila and Ben were playing in the garden. They liked to dig holes and look for bugs. They found a big worm, a shiny beetle and a funny spider. They put them in a jar and showed them to Mom.

"Look, Mom, we found some friends!" Lila said.

Mom smiled and said, "They are very interesting, but you should let them go soon. They need to live in the soil and the plants, not in a jar."

"OK, Mom, we will," Ben said.

They went back to the garden and dug some more holes. Then they saw something moving under a rock. They lifted the rock and saw a small, brown animal with a long nose and tiny eyes. It was a mole.

"Wow, what is that?" Lila asked.

"It's a mole," Ben said. "It lives under the ground and eats worms and bugs."

"Can we keep it?" Lila asked.

"No, we can't," Ben said. "It's not a pet. It's wild and it might bite us. And it's ugly."

The mole heard Ben and felt sad. It did not think it was ugly. It thought it was beautiful and clever. It could dig tunnels and find food and sense vibrations. It did not like the bright light and the loud noises. It wanted to go back to its home.

"Please, let me go," the mole said in a soft voice.

Lila and Ben heard the mole and were surprised. They did not know moles could talk.

"Did you hear that?" Lila asked.

"Yes, I did," Ben said.

They looked at the mole and saw that it was scared and unhappy. They felt sorry for it.

"OK, we will let you go," Lila said. "We are sorry we bothered you. You are not ugly. You are special."

"Thank you," the mole said. "You are kind."

Lila and Ben gently put the mole back under the rock and covered it with soil. They wiped their hands and went to find Mom. They told her about the mole and what it said. Mom hugged them and said, "You did the right thing. You are good children."

Lily liked to eat avocado. She liked the green and soft part inside. She did not like the brown and hard part outside. She used a spoon to scoop the avocado from the skin.

One day, Lily's mom gave her a white bowl with avocado and cheese. Lily was happy. She said, "Thank you, mom. I love avocado and cheese."

She started to eat with her spoon. But then she saw something in her bowl. It was a small black thing. Lily did not know what it was. She did not like it. She said, "Ew, what is this?"

Her mom looked at her bowl. She said, "That is a seed, Lily. It is from the avocado. It is not for eating. You can leave it in the bowl."

Lily did not want to leave it in the bowl. She did not want to see it. She said, "No, mom. I don't like it. It is yucky. I want to quit."

Her mom said, "Lily, don't quit. You still have a lot of avocado and cheese. They are yummy. The seed is not yucky. It is just different. You can try to touch it. It is smooth and round."

Lily was curious. She used her spoon to poke the seed. It was smooth and round. She said, "It is smooth and round. Can I play with it?"

Her mom said, "Yes, you can play with it. But don't put it in your mouth. It is not for eating. It is for growing new avocados."

Lily smiled. She said, "Okay, mom. I will play with it. And I will eat the avocado and cheese. They are yummy."

She finished her bowl. She was happy. She said, "Thank you, mom. I like avocado and cheese. And I like the seed. It is fun."

Once upon a time, there was a little bunny who wanted to be independent. He wanted to do things on his own, without help from his mommy or daddy. One day, the bunny saw an envelope on the ground. He wanted to pick it up, but he couldn't stand up on his hind legs.

The bunny felt sad and frustrated, but he didn't give up. He practiced standing every day until he could finally stand on his own two feet. One day, he saw another bunny who was struggling to stand up with a heavy load of carrots. The independent bunny went over to help him and together, they carried the carrots to their burrows.

From that day on, the independent bunny knew that it was good to be able to stand on his own, but it was even better to help others who couldn't stand on their own. He felt happy and proud of himself for being able to help others. The moral of the story is that being independent is good, but helping others is even better.

Once upon a time, there were two little brothers, Mark and Tom. Every day, Mark and Tom played together happily. One day, Mark wanted to mix a special potion. He asked Tom to help him. But Tom was worried about the potion, so he said no.

Mark was sad, but he still wanted to mix the potion. So he decided to go ahead and mix it all by himself. He took some water, some leaves and a few other things.

The potion smelled strong and strange. Suddenly, a bright light surrounded Mark and the room. When the light disappeared, Mark had vanished!

Tom was so scared that he ran away. He looked for an exit and managed to escape.

The moral of this story is that one should be thoughtful and think before doing something. Just because something is fun or exciting doesn't mean it's a good idea. Sometimes it brings bad consequences.

When Tweet arrived at Flutter's house, she was out of breath. She told Flutter all about the scary bird and how she had flown over the cliff to get to her house. Flutter listened carefully and then told Tweet that she had seen the scary bird before. She knew how to avoid it.

From then on, Tweet and Flutter always flew around the cliff instead of over it. They were happy to have each other to tell their secrets and keep each other safe.

One day, they see a big worm on the rock. It is brown and slimy. Lily screams and runs away. Ben laughs and picks up the worm. He says, "Look, Lily, it is a friend. It is not scary. It is soft and wiggly."

Lily does not like the worm. She says, "No, Ben, it is not a friend. It is disgusting. It is dirty and icky. Put it down. It will make you sick."

Ben does not listen. He says, "No, Lily, it is fun. It tickles my hand. I want to keep it. I will name it Wally."

Lily shakes her head. She says, "You are silly, Ben. You cannot keep a worm. It needs soil and water. It does not belong on the rock. And you need to wash your hand. Come on, let's go to the shower."

Ben makes a face. He says, "I do not want to go to the shower. The shower is cold and wet. It is not fun. I want to stay with Wally."

Lily grabs Ben's hand. She says, "You have to go to the shower, Ben. Mommy said so. She said we have to be clean and tidy. And Wally has to go back to the garden. He will be happier there. Come on, Ben, please."

Ben sighs. He says, "Okay, Lily, fine. But I will miss Wally. He is a good worm. Bye, Wally. See you later."

Lily and Ben go to the shower. They wash their hands and faces. They rinse off the dirt and the slime. They feel fresh and happy. They hug each other and say, "We love you, Wally. But we love each other more."

They played with Max for a while, and he showed them how he could freeze other things, like rocks, leaves, and bugs. Lila and Ben thought he was fun and friendly, but they also felt a little scared of his power. They wondered what would happen if he froze them. They hoped he would not do that.

Tom is a smart boy. He likes to learn new things. He has a tutor who comes to his house every week. The tutor helps him with reading and writing and math.

One day, Tom is playing with his toys when the tutor arrives. He hears the doorbell and runs to open it. He is happy to see the tutor.

"Hello, Tom. Are you ready for our lesson?" the tutor asks.

"Yes, I am. Come in, please," Tom says.

They go to the living room, where Tom has a table and a chair and some books. The tutor takes out a paper and a pencil. He writes some words on the paper.

"Tom, can you read these words for me?" the tutor says.

Tom looks at the paper. He knows some of the words, but not all of them. He tries to sound them out.

"Cat, dog, sun, fun, red, bed," he reads.

"Very good, Tom. You are doing well. Now, can you write these words on another paper?" the tutor says.

Tom nods. He takes another paper and a pencil. He starts to write the words. He writes cat, dog, sun, fun, red, but then he stops. He forgets how to write bed. He looks at the tutor's paper, but he can't see it well. He feels sad.

"I forget how to write bed," he says.

The tutor smiles. He moves his paper closer to Tom.

"That's okay, Tom. Everyone forgets sometimes. Look at my paper. Can you see the letters in bed?" he says.

Tom looks at the paper. He sees the letters b, e, and d. He remembers how to write them.

"Oh, I see. B, e, d. Bed," he says.

He writes bed on his paper. He shows it to the tutor.

"Good job, Tom. You remembered. You are a smart boy. I am proud of you," the tutor says.

Tom smiles. He feels happy. He likes the tutor. He likes to learn new things. He does not want to forget.

Once upon a time there was a small girl named Lucy. She was happy and wanted to explore the world.

One day, Lucy found a valley that she had never seen before. She decided to explore the valley and when she reached the bottom, she noticed it was hot.

Lucy asked a nearby butterfly, "Why is it so hot in this valley?" The butterfly explained that inside the valley it was getting too hot and she had to solve the problem.

Lucy thought and thought and came up with an idea. She made a fan out of some sticks and some leaves she had found and put it by the entrance of the valley. The fan blew the hot air away and cooled the valley down.

The butterfly was very pleased and thanked Lucy. From then on Lucy explored the valley with the butterfly and they had many great adventures.

Tom and Mia are twins. They like to play with their toys. But sometimes they fight over them. One day, they find a big car in the garage. It is red and shiny. It has four wheels and a horn.

"Wow, look at this car!" Tom says. "I want to drive it!"

"No, I want to drive it!" Mia says. "You always get the best toys!"

They both run to the car and try to get in. But the car is too small for both of them. They push and pull and shout.

"Let me in, let me in!" Tom says.

"Go away, go away!" Mia says.

They are very selfish. They do not want to share the car.

Dad hears the noise and comes to the garage. He sees Tom and Mia fighting over the car. He is not happy.

"What are you doing?" he asks. "Why are you fighting over the car?"

"Because it is mine!" Tom says.

"No, it is mine!" Mia says.

Dad shakes his head. He has an idea.

"Listen, kids," he says. "The car is not yours. It is mine. I bought it for a special reason. Do you want to know what it is?"

Tom and Mia stop fighting. They are curious.

"What is it, Dad?" they ask.

Dad smiles. He opens the trunk of the car. He shows them a big bag of toys. There are dolls, cars, balls, books, and more.

"I bought this car to fill it with toys," he says. "I want to give them to the children who have no toys. They are very poor and sad. They need some joy in their lives. Do you want to help me?"

Tom and Mia look at the bag of toys. They look at each other. They feel ashamed. They have so many toys, but they are not happy. They are selfish.

They nod at Dad. They say sorry to each other. They hug.

"Yes, Dad," they say. "We want to help you. We want to share our toys with the children who have no toys. We want to make them happy."

Dad is proud of them. He hugs them back.

"Good," he says. "Let's go then. Let's fill the car with toys and drive to the orphanage. It will be a fun and kind adventure."

Tom and Mia smile. They are excited. They help Dad fill the car with toys. They get in the car and buckle up. They honk the horn.

"Beep beep!" they say.

They drive away. They are not selfish anymore. They are generous. They are happy.

Once upon a time, there was a small flower called Blossom. Blossom was born into a garden full of other vibrant flowers, but it was the weakest of the bunch. Everyday, Blossom looked around and saw how the other flowers were blooming and wished that it had the strength to bloom too.

"Why can't I be like the other flowers?" Blossom asked one day. "I just want to be able to bloom too!"

The other flowers in the garden heard Blossom's cries and decided to help it. "We can help you," said the other flowers. They gathered around the weakest flower and gathered their energy to help it bloom.

Slowly, Blossom began to open up. A beautiful pink petal reached up to the sky and then another one on the other side. Before long, Blossom had bloomed into a beautiful flower and it looked so happy.

The garden was filled with joy and everyone was amazed at the sight of the little flower that had bloomed from the weakest side of the garden. From that moment onward, Blossom never felt weak again.

John stood and looked angry. He folded his arms and said he wanted it. Chloe just shook her head. John started feeling frustrated and he kicked the ground.

John's mom saw the children from a distance and joined them. She asked what was happening and they told her. She looked at the delicious cupcake and smiled.

Then she said, "I can give you something just as delicious, John. Then everyone will be happy." She bought John an ice cream cone and everyone enjoyed it.

Sara and Lily were sisters who liked to play together. One day, they found a bottle of perfume in their mom's room. It smelled like flowers and candy.

"Can we try it?" Sara asked.

"OK, but be careful. Mom said perfume is for special days, not for everyday," Lily said.

They sprayed some perfume on their wrists and necks. They felt very pretty and grown-up.

"Let's go show Dad," Sara said.

They ran downstairs to find their dad in the kitchen. He was making pancakes for breakfast.

"Hi, girls. You look very nice today," he said.

He hugged them and kissed their cheeks. Then he smelled something.

"What is that?" he asked.

"It's perfume, Dad. We found it in Mom's room. Do you like it?" Lily said.

Dad smiled. He was a compassionate dad. He knew the girls were curious and wanted to have fun.

"It's very nice, but it's also very strong. Maybe you used too much. How about we wash it off and save it for another day?" he said.

"OK, Dad. We're sorry. We didn't mean to make you sneeze," Sara said.

They went to the bathroom and washed their faces and hands. They closed the bottle of perfume and put it back in Mom's room.

They felt a little sad, but they also felt happy. They knew their dad loved them and wanted them to be happy too.

They went back to the kitchen and ate pancakes with their dad. They told him stories and jokes. They laughed and hugged.

They forgot about the perfume. They had a special day anyway.

After a while, Grandma brought out some toys. All the kids ran over to see their favorite toys. They all wanted to play with them.

Suddenly, one of the kids found a toy hammer. He grabbed it and started to destroy all of the other toys. He had so much fun smashing them!

The kids started to cry, but Grandma was not mad. She just said that it was an important lesson. We should always be careful with our toys and not destroy them.

The kids all agreed and the party went on. Soon, everyone was excited and playing again. Grandma was glad that the party was happy once more.

Once upon a time, there was a little girl named Lily. She loved to run around and play outside. One day, she put on her favorite red shoes and ran outside to play. Her shoes were so comfy and she loved how fast she could run in them.

As she was running, she saw a little harmless bug on the ground. She thought it was so cute and wanted to pick it up. But just as she was about to, she heard a loud buzzing noise. It was a bee! Lily got scared and started to run away as fast as she could in her speedy shoes.

When she got home, Lily's mom asked her why she was running so fast. Lily told her about the bee and how she was scared. Her mom hugged her and told her that bees are harmless if you don't bother them. From that day on, Lily knew to be careful around bees, but she still loved her speedy red shoes.

"Look, there is a red bird!" Tom says. "It is very pretty. I want to catch it."

He runs after the bird, but the bird flies away. Tom tries again and again, but the bird is too fast.

"This is difficult," Tom says. "The bird is smart. It knows I want to catch it."

Mia sees a blue bird on a bench. She walks slowly and quietly. She holds out her hand with some bread. The bird hops closer and closer. It pecks at the bread. Mia smiles and gently grabs the bird.

"I win!" Mia says. "I catch a bird. It is very soft. I will call it Blue."

Tom comes back and sees Mia with the bird. He feels sad and angry.

"That is not fair!" Tom says. "You cheat. You use bread. I want a bird too."

Mia shakes her head. "No, I do not cheat. I am clever. You are loud. The birds do not like loud. You can share my bird. We can be friends."

Tom thinks for a moment. He does not want to be mean. He wants to be friends. He nods and smiles.

"OK, we can share. Your bird is nice. Can I hold it?"

Mia nods and gives Tom the bird. The bird chirps and flaps its wings. Tom and Mia laugh and hug. They are happy. They have a bird.

Once there was a frog. He was bright green and he had big eyes. One day he was hopping around and he saw a leaf. The leaf was big and green. It looked great. So the frog jumped on to it. The leaf started to float away. The frog was so excited.

He bounced on the leaf. It felt like he was flying. The wind blew and the leaf swayed. Soon the leaf came to rest on a big pond. The frog jumped off the leaf and into the cool water. He swam around and around the pond. It was so much fun.

Soon the frog jumped back onto the leaf. He sailed across the pond. He felt like he was going on a great adventure. The leaf took him to a nearby tree. The frog hopped off the leaf and went looking for lunch. He was so happy and full of fun. The end.

She had to clean her room. All morning she had been putting off this dull task. But now it was time, Sarah knew. She sighed and trudged up the hill, her feet dragging.

She opened the door and stopped for a moment. Looking at the room, Sarah knew it was going to be a struggle. She decided to start small, so she grabbed a toy and put it in the toy box. She quickly stuffed three more inside, feeling triumphant.

But soon, she began to tire. The next task seemed nearly impossible. But Sarah remembered all the fun she had while playing at the park. She found her motivation, and the dull task didn't seem so bad.

So Sarah worked hard. She scrubbed and swept and folded and put away her toys. After what seemed like an eternity, the task was complete. Pleased with her hard work, Sarah left her room with a smile.

Once upon a time there was a small rabbit named Fluffy. Fluffy was very cute and had big, floppy ears.

One day, Fluffy was hopping along through the forest on a very foggy day. The fog was so thick that Fluffy couldn't see very far. He hopped and hopped for a long time, until he stumbled across a pretty little meadow.

Fluffy was very excited when he saw the meadow. He hopped up and down, looking for something to do. Suddenly, he found a berry bush! Fluffy had never seen a berry bush before. He could hardly believe his luck.

"I have to have these berries!", Fluffy said to himself. He hopped over and grabbed a few of the berries. But just as he was about to take a bite, a loud voice yelled: "Stop!"

Fluffy was so startled that he jumped back. There was a small woman standing in front of him. She had gray hair and pointy ears. She was a fairy!

"You can have these berries if you promise to yield your first harvest to me when the time comes," the fairy said.

Fluffy thought it over and agreed. The fairy smiled, thanked him, and disappeared into the fog.

Fluffy left the meadow with a pocket full of pretty berries, proud that he had yielded for the fairy.

"What's wrong, Lily?" her mom asked.

"It's okay, sweetie. Lightning is just a big flash of light in the sky. It's loud, but it won't hurt you," her mom said, trying to calm her down.

Lily felt better knowing that lightning wasn't going to hurt her. She took a deep breath and looked up at the quiet sky. She felt safe knowing her mom was there to protect her.

"Maybe," the man says. "We come to the park sometimes. Maybe you can find us again."

"Why did you do that, Ben?" Lily asked. She was angry and sad.

"I wanted to play with your toys and read your books. But I could not put them back. I did not know where they belong," Ben said. He looked down.

"OK, Lily. Thank you. I'm sorry. I love you," Ben said. He hugged her.

"Look, my tower is taller than yours!" Lily said, putting more sand on top of her spade.

"No, it's not!" Tom said, doing the same with his spade. "Mine is taller and stronger!"

They kept adding more and more sand, until their spades were too heavy to lift. They tried to pull them out, but they were stuck.

"Help!" Lily cried. "My spade is trapped!"

"Me too!" Tom said. "I can't get my spade out!"

They pulled and pulled, but nothing happened. They started to cry.

A man was walking by with his dog. He saw the children crying and came over.

"What's wrong, little ones?" he asked.

"Our spades are stuck in the sand!" Lily and Tom said.

The man smiled and bent down. He took hold of their spades and pulled them out with ease.

"Here you go," he said, handing them their spades. "You were trying to make a castle, right?"

"Yes, but we made it too big and our spades got stuck," Lily said.

"Well, sometimes less is more," the man said. "Why don't you try to make a smaller castle, but with more details? Like windows and doors and flags?"

"That sounds fun!" Tom said.

"Thank you, mister!" Lily said.

"You're welcome," the man said. "Have fun, but be careful not to dig too deep. The sand can be bitter if you taste it."

He waved and walked away with his dog.

Lily and Tom looked at each other and smiled. They decided to make a smaller castle, but with more details. They used their spades to carve windows and doors and flags. They were happy and proud of their castle. They did not stop until it was done.

Her mom nodded and Jane ran to catch the grasshopper. She was so excited that she was jumping up and down with joy!

The end.

Mia smiled. Suddenly, Ben appeared at the top of the hill. He asked for her forgiveness, and Mia said yes. The two young friends hugged each other. They enjoyed the scenic view, together.

Once upon a time there was a little girl who loved to pick different things from the garden. She spent her day eagerly picking flowers and leaves. One day she stumbled upon something different from the usual things she picked. This was a pattern!

The little girl was so excited. She picked it carefully and brought it back home. She was mesmerized by its regular structure and marvelled at its beauty. She kept it safe in her jar of treasures and continued to admire it.

The little girl soon learnt that having even the simplest of joys can bring pleasure if they were picked with care. The moral of the story is to appreciate and treasure things that are picked regularly regardless of how small they may seem.

Lily and Ben were best friends. They liked to play in the park every day. They liked to swing on the swings, slide on the slides, and run on the grass. But they did not like the maze. The maze was big and dark and scary. They were fearful of the maze.

One day, Lily and Ben were swinging on the swings. They saw a new boy in the park. He was swinging on the swing next to them. He had a big smile and a red hat. He said hello to them.

"Hi, I'm Tom. Do you want to play with me?" he asked.

"Sure, we can play with you. What do you want to play?" Lily said.

"Let's play in the maze. It's fun and exciting. Come on, follow me!" Tom said.

He jumped off the swing and ran to the maze. Lily and Ben looked at each other. They did not want to play in the maze. They were fearful of the maze.

"Tom, wait! We don't like the maze. It's big and dark and scary. We want to play something else." Ben said.

But Tom did not hear them. He was already inside the maze. He was laughing and shouting.

"Come on, don't be scared. The maze is not scary. It's just a game. You can find your way out. It's easy. Trust me!" he said.

Lily and Ben did not trust him. They were fearful of the maze. But they did not want to lose their new friend. They wanted to play with him. They decided to be brave and try the maze.

They held hands and walked slowly to the maze. They entered the maze. They saw many paths and walls and turns. They did not know which way to go. They tried to follow Tom's voice, but it was hard to hear. They felt lost and alone. They were fearful of the maze.

They wished they were back on the swings. They wished they had never met Tom. They wished they could get out of the maze. They started to cry.

"Help! Help! We want to get out! We don't like the maze!" they cried.

Then they heard a familiar voice. It was Tom. He had found them. He had a big smile and a red hat. He was holding a map.

"Don't cry, don't cry. I'm here to help you. I have a map. I know the way out. Follow me!" he said.

He took their hands and led them through the maze. He showed them the right paths and turns. He made jokes and songs. He made them laugh and smile. He was not fearful of the maze. He was fun and kind.

Soon they reached the exit. They saw the sun and the sky and the park. They felt happy and relieved. They were out of the maze.

"See, that was not so bad. That was fun and exciting. You did it! You were brave and smart. You should be proud of yourselves!" Tom said.

He hugged them and gave them the map.

"Here, you can keep the map. Next time, you can play in the maze again. Or you can play something else. I don't mind. I just want to be your friend." he said.

Lily and Ben smiled and thanked him. They looked at the map. They looked at the maze. They looked at each other. They were not fearful of the maze anymore. They were curious and adventurous. They wanted to play with Tom again.

They decided to give the maze another try. They followed the map and explored the maze. They had fun and exciting. They were friends.

Once upon a time, there was a nosy fox who wanted to see what everyone else was doing. One day, the fox happened to notice a group of animals playing a game. The fox was curious and he wanted to join in, but the other animals said no.

The fox was all alone and he was feeling sad, when the wise owl flew by and said, "You can't play their game, but you can play your own game."

The fox was confused, he didn't know how to make a game. The owl said, "You need to find something that only you know and make a game out of it."

The fox was so excited! He immediately began searching for something that only he knew and finally, he found a perfect idea.
The fox created a game and the other animals loved it.

Tom and Lily were twins who liked to play with different things. Tom loved to look at tiny things with his microscope. He could see bugs, hairs, and even dust. Lily liked to draw and paint with her crayons and brushes. She could make colorful pictures of flowers, animals, and stars.

One day, Tom found a new thing to look at with his microscope. It was a shiny rock that he picked up from the park. He put it on the slide and turned on the light. He saw many sparkles and shapes inside the rock. He was very happy and excited.

"Look, Lily, look!" he shouted. "I found a magic rock! It has so many pretty things inside!"

Lily came over and looked at the rock. She saw the sparkles and shapes, too. But she was not happy and excited. She was jealous. She wanted to have a magic rock, too. She wanted to look at it with her own microscope. But she did not have one. She only had crayons and brushes.

"Tom, can I have your microscope?" she asked. "I want to see the magic rock better."

"No, Lily, you can't," Tom said. "This is my microscope. I got it for my birthday. You can use your crayons and brushes. They are fun, too."

Lily felt angry and sad. She did not want to use her crayons and brushes. She wanted to use Tom's microscope. She grabbed the microscope and tried to pull it away from Tom. Tom held on to the microscope and tried to push Lily away. They both started to yell and cry.

"Stop, stop, stop!" their mom said. She heard the noise and came into the room. She saw Tom and Lily fighting over the microscope. She was not happy. She took the microscope and the rock from them. She put them on the shelf.

"Tom, Lily, you are both being very naughty," she said. "You need to share and be nice to each other. You have many things to play with. You don't need to fight over one thing. Now, you both need to rest and calm down. Go to your beds and take a nap."

Tom and Lily did not want to go to their beds. They wanted to play with the microscope and the rock. But they knew they had to listen to their mom. They went to their beds and lay down. They were still feeling jealous and angry. But they were also feeling tired and sorry. They closed their eyes and fell asleep. They dreamed of sparkles and shapes.

The little girl hugged her little friend and said, "We had such a great time today!"

The little boy smiled and replied, "Yes, it was the best day ever!"

And they laughed together, a cheerful little laugh, one that only the best of friends could make.

Once upon a time, there was a boy named Timmy. Timmy loved to eat candy every day. His mom always told him that he needed to eat healthy food, but he didn't want to listen. One day, Timmy found a magic bean in a sack. He ate the bean and suddenly he started to shrink!

Timmy was so small that he could fit inside the sack. He climbed inside and found himself in a magical land. There he met a friendly giant who said, "Hello little one, what brings you here?" Timmy explained what had happened and the giant said, "You need to eat healthy food to grow big and strong again."

Timmy realized that the giant was right. He asked the giant if he could have some of his healthy food. The giant gave Timmy a big carrot and some fresh apples. Timmy ate the healthy food and soon he grew back to his normal size. Timmy thanked the giant and went back home to tell his mom all about his adventure. From that day on, Timmy ate healthy food every day and never wanted to shrink again.

Billy said, "I saw some radishes in Farmer Joe's garden. But be careful, he doesn't like animals taking his vegetables."

Benny thanked Billy and went to Farmer Joe's garden. He saw some radishes, but they were too high for him to reach. He leaned against a big rock and tried to jump, but he still couldn't reach them.

Just then, Farmer Joe came out and saw Benny. "What are you doing here?" he asked.

Benny said, "I want some radishes, but they're too high. Can you help me?"

Farmer Joe smiled and said, "Sure, I have a ladder available. Let me get it for you." He got the ladder and helped Benny pick some radishes.

Benny was so happy and thanked Farmer Joe. He went back to his garden and shared the radishes with Billy. They both had a yummy snack and were happy they helped each other.

"Johnny, don't touch that worm!" said his mom.

Johnny didn't listen. He picked up the worm, and put it in his pocket. His mom scolded him and told him to put the worm back on the ground.

"No," said Johnny. "I want to keep it."

His mom was starting to get angry. "Johnny," she said, "I recommend that you put that worm back on the ground. It's not safe to keep it."

Johnny thought about it for a moment. But then he said, "No, I want to keep the worm."

His mom was getting frustrated. "Johnny, please put it down. It's not safe to keep it," she said again.

But Johnny refused to listen. In the end, his mom had to take the worm out of his pocket, and put it back on the ground. Johnny watched as the big worm disappeared into the tall grass.

Lily and Max were twins who liked to play in the garden. One day, they saw a big white thing in the ground. It looked like a flower, but it was not pretty or colorful.

"What is that?" Lily asked.

"It is a cauliflower," Max said. He had learned the word from their mom.

"Can we pick it?" Lily asked.

"No, we have to wait until it is ready," Max said. He wanted to show the cauliflower to their mom and dad.

But Lily was curious and impatient. She pulled the cauliflower out of the ground. It was heavy and hard.

"Look, I have it!" Lily said. She ran to the house with the cauliflower.

Max was angry and sad. He chased after Lily. He wanted to put the cauliflower back in the ground.

"Stop, Lily, stop!" Max shouted. "You are not supposed to do that!"

But Lily was too fast. She reached the house before Max. She showed the cauliflower to their mom and dad.

"Look what I found in the garden!" Lily said.

Mom and dad looked at the cauliflower. They looked at Lily. They looked at Max.

They were not happy.

"Lily, you should not have picked the cauliflower," mom said. "It was not ready yet. You have to be patient and respectful of nature."

"Lily, you should not have run away from me," Max said. "I wanted to show the cauliflower to mom and dad too. You have to be fair and share with your brother."

Lily felt sorry. She realized she had made a mistake. She hugged Max and gave him the cauliflower.

"I am sorry, Max," Lily said. "You can show the cauliflower to mom and dad. I will wait for the next one to grow."

Max smiled and hugged Lily back. He showed the cauliflower to mom and dad. They praised him for being smart and kind.

Lily and Max learned a lesson. They learned to be patient, respectful, fair and share. They played in the garden again, but this time they did not pick anything until it was ready. They enjoyed watching the cauliflower and other plants grow. They were happy.

Lily liked to play in the garden. She liked to dig in the dirt and look for bugs. She found a big black beetle with long legs and shiny wings. She was very happy. She put the beetle in a jar and ran to show her mom.

"Look, mom, look what I found!" Lily said. "Can I keep it? Please, please, please?"

Mom looked at the jar and frowned. She did not like bugs. She thought they were icky and dirty. She did not want them in the house.

"No, Lily, you can't keep it," mom said. "It's not a pet. It belongs in the garden. You have to let it go."

Lily felt sad and angry. She loved her beetle. She wanted to keep it. She did not want to let it go.

"But mom, I promise I will take good care of it," Lily said. "I will give it water and leaves and a name. I will be nice to it. Please, mom, please."

Mom shook her head. She did not change her mind. She said Lily had to let the beetle go or she would be in trouble.

Lily did not listen. She hid the jar under her bed and hoped mom would not find it. She thought she was clever. She thought she could keep her beetle.

But she was wrong. The next day, when she came home from school, she saw the jar on the table. The lid was off. The beetle was gone. Mom was waiting for her with a stern look.

"Lily, what did you do?" mom asked. "You broke your promise. You lied to me. You did a bad thing."

Lily felt sorry and scared. She did not mean to do a bad thing. She just wanted to keep her beetle. She looked for it in the garden, but she could not find it. She lost her beetle and she made mom mad.

She started to cry. She said she was sorry. She said she would not do it again.

Mom hugged her and said she forgave her. She said she loved her. She said she understood. She said she would help her find another bug to play with in the garden. But she said she had to let it go when she was done.

Lily nodded. She learned her lesson. She said she would keep her promise. She said she would let the bug go. She said she loved mom too. She said she was happy.

He put the branch in the water and tried to push it with his hands. But the branch was too heavy and it sank.

"Oh no, Ben, your boat is gone!" Lily said, feeling sorry for her brother.

Ben was sad. He wanted to get his branch back. He took off his shoes and socks and rolled up his pants. He stepped into the pond and felt the cold water on his feet.

"I can swim and get it!" he said, bravely.

But Ben was not a good swimmer. He was clumsy and he splashed a lot. He could not reach the branch. He only got wet and muddy.

"Ben, come back, it's too deep!" Lily shouted, worried.

She ran to the edge of the pond and reached out her hand. Ben saw her and grabbed her hand. She pulled him out of the water and hugged him.

"Are you okay, Ben?" she asked, softly.

"I'm okay, Lily, thank you," he said, shivering.

They walked back to their mom, who was sitting on a bench. She saw them and smiled.

"What happened, my darlings?" she asked, kindly.

"We were playing with a branch, but it sank and Ben tried to swim and get it, but he couldn't and he got wet and Lily helped him and we're sorry, mom," they said, quickly.

Mom laughed and wrapped them in a towel.

"It's okay, my darlings, I'm glad you're safe and you helped each other. But next time, be careful and don't go into the pond without me, okay?" she said, gently.

"Okay, mom," they said, nodding.

They snuggled with mom and watched the fish and the ducks swim in the water. They forgot about the branch. They were happy.

Tim and Kim are twins. They like to play in the park. One day, they see a gray cat in a tree. The cat is scared and meows. Tim and Kim want to help the cat.

They look for a ladder, but they do not find one. They look for a rope, but they do not find one. They look for a big stick, but they do not find one. They are sad and do not know what to do.

Then, they see a big dog. The dog is tough and strong. He can run fast and jump high. Tim and Kim have an idea. They call the dog and show him the cat. The dog barks and runs to the tree. He jumps and catches the cat in his mouth. He brings the cat to Tim and Kim.

The cat is not hurt. He is happy and purrs. Tim and Kim are happy too. They pet the cat and the dog. They thank the dog for his rescue. The dog wags his tail and licks their faces. They are all friends. They play in the park until it is time to go home.

Tom and Mia were friends who liked to play with clay. They made many things with clay, like animals, cars, and houses. One day, they decided to make a volcano with clay. They used a big bottle as the base and covered it with brown clay. They made a hole at the top and put some red clay inside.

"Look, our volcano is ready!" Tom said. "Let's pretend it can erupt and make lava!"

"How do we make lava?" Mia asked.

"We need something that can melt and be hot and red," Tom said. He looked around and saw a box of crayons. He took some red crayons and broke them into pieces. He put them in a small pot and asked Mia to help him carry it to the kitchen.

"Can we use the stove?" Mia asked.

"Yes, but we have to be careful. It is very hot and can burn us," Tom said. He turned on the stove and put the pot on it. He watched as the crayons started to melt and become liquid.

"Wow, it looks like lava!" Mia said.

"Let's take it to our volcano and make it erupt!" Tom said. He used a big spoon to scoop some of the melted crayons and poured it into the hole of the volcano. The red liquid flowed down the sides of the volcano and made a mess on the floor.

"It looks so cool!" Mia said.

"It looks so rich!" Tom said.

They heard a loud voice from the living room. It was Tom's mom.

"Tom! Mia! What are you doing in the kitchen? Come here right now!"

Tom and Mia looked at each other and ran to the living room. They saw Tom's mom holding a newspaper. She looked very angry.

"Look at this! You ruined my newspaper with your crayons! It was a very important newspaper! It had a lot of rich people and their houses in it! How could you do this?"

Tom and Mia felt very sorry. They did not mean to ruin the newspaper. They only wanted to play with their volcano.

"We are sorry, mom. We did not know it was your newspaper. We were making lava for our volcano," Tom said.

"Your volcano? What volcano?" Tom's mom asked.

Tom and Mia took her to the kitchen and showed her their volcano. They explained how they made it with clay and crayons.

Tom's mom looked at their volcano and the mess on the floor. She was still angry, but she also saw how creative and clever they were.

"I see. You made a very nice volcano, but you also made a very big mess. You have to clean it up and apologize to me. And no more playing with crayons on the stove. It is very dangerous. Do you understand?"

Tom and Mia nodded. They said they were sorry and hugged Tom's mom. They cleaned up the mess and put away their volcano. They learned their lesson and promised to be more careful next time.

"But it's so shiny and pretty," Anna said.

"And it has a picture of a man with a hat," Ben said.

Mom explained, "That's George Washington. He was a wise man who helped our country a long time ago. He was the first president. He's on the quarter because he's important."

Lily was sick and had to go to the hospital. She did not like the hospital. It was big and loud and scary. She wanted to go home and play with her toys.

A nurse came to see Lily. She had a white coat and a kind smile. She said, "Hello, Lily. I'm here to help you feel better. I need to check your temperature and give you some medicine. Can you be brave for me?"

Lily nodded, but she felt nervous. The nurse put a stick in her mouth and looked at a watch. Then she took a syringe from a tray. Lily saw the needle and started to cry. She did not want the needle. It would hurt.

The nurse said, "I know, Lily. It's not fun, but it's very important. The medicine will make you strong and fight the germs. It will be over soon, I promise. Do you want me to hold your hand?"

Lily nodded again, and the nurse held her hand. She felt a little better. The nurse said, "You're doing great, Lily. You're very brave. Do you know what this medicine reminds me of?"

Lily shook her head, still crying.

The nurse said, "It reminds me of strawberry jam. It's red and sweet and good for you. Do you like strawberry jam?"

Lily sniffed and said, "Yes, I do. I like it on toast."

The nurse said, "Me too. Maybe when you get better, you can have some toast with strawberry jam. How does that sound?"

Lily smiled a little and said, "That sounds nice."

The nurse said, "Good. Now, let's count to three and then I'll give you the medicine, okay? One, two, three!"

The nurse pushed the syringe and Lily felt a pinch. She whimpered, but it was over quickly. The nurse said, "You did it, Lily! You're amazing! I'm so proud of you!"

Lily felt proud too, but also embarrassed. She had cried in front of the nurse. She said, "I'm sorry, I was scared."

The nurse said, "That's okay, Lily. Everyone gets scared sometimes. Even me. But you were very brave and strong. You don't have to be sorry. You have to be happy. You're getting better every day."

Lily hugged the nurse and said, "Thank you, nurse. You're very nice. You make me happy."

The nurse hugged her back and said, "You're very welcome, Lily. You make me happy too."

Sara and Ben are twins. They like to eat yogurt for breakfast. Mom gives them each a cup of yogurt and a spoon. Sara likes strawberry yogurt. Ben likes blueberry yogurt.

Sara looks at Ben's yogurt. She thinks it is beautiful. It is purple and has little dots. She wants to try it. She says to Ben, "Can I have some of your yogurt?"

Ben says, "No, this is my yogurt. You have your own yogurt. It is pink and has seeds. You like it."

Sara says, "But I want to taste your yogurt. It looks yummy. Please, Ben, please."

Ben says, "No, Sara, no. Go away. Leave me alone."

Sara gets angry. She pulls Ben's yogurt cup from his hand. Ben pulls it back. They pull and pull. The yogurt cup breaks. The yogurt spills on the table and on their clothes. They both cry.

Mom hears them cry. She comes to the kitchen. She sees the mess. She is not happy. She says, "What happened here? Why did you pull the yogurt cup? Why did you spill the yogurt?"

Sara and Ben say, "We are sorry, Mom. We wanted to share the yogurt. But we pulled too hard. We made a mistake."

Mom says, "It's okay to share, but you have to ask nicely and wait for an answer. You don't pull things from each other. That is not nice. That is rude. You have to be gentle and respectful. Do you understand?"

Sara and Ben say, "Yes, Mom, we understand. We are sorry. We love you."

Mom says, "I love you too. But now you have to clean up the mess. And then you have to change your clothes. And then you can have some more yogurt. But this time, no pulling, okay?"

Sara and Ben say, "Okay, Mom, okay. No pulling. Thank you for the yogurt. It is delicious."

We love to sing. We love the subway." Mom hugs them and says, "I love you. You make me happy." They reach their grandma's stop. They get off the subway and wave goodbye to the people. They go to see their grandma. She is very happy to see them. She gives them cookies and milk. They tell her about their subway adventure. They sing the ABC song for her. She says, "You are very intelligent. You are very good singers. You are very sweet." They hug her and say, "We love you, grandma. You make us happy." They have a wonderful day.

Once upon a time there was a little duck. It was a happy duck who liked to splash in the pond. Then one day, it saw something shiny on the water - it was a big, ugly print. The print was big and ugly and the duck was scared.

But it didn't stay scared for too long. It remembered how much fun it had splashing in the pond. So it took a deep breath and it bravely jumped into the water. As soon as it did, it made a big splash that made the ugly print go away. It couldn't believe it had been so brave.

The little duck was very happy now. It had been brave and the ugly print was gone. And it could splash whenever it wanted. So the little duck splashed and splashed and splashed in the pond, and it stayed happy forever.

Tom and Sam are brothers. They like to help their dad in the kitchen. Dad is a cook. He makes yummy food for people. He works hard every day.

One day, Tom and Sam want to work with dad. They ask him, "Dad, can we work with you? We want to learn how to cook."

Dad smiles and says, "Sure, you can work with me. But you have to be careful. Cooking is fun, but it can also be dangerous. You have to follow my rules."

Dad gives Tom and Sam aprons and hats. He shows them how to wash their hands and the vegetables. He tells them to cut the carrots with a knife. He says, "The knife is sharp. You have to hold it with two hands. And you have to cut slowly and gently. Don't cut your fingers. And don't touch the stove. It is hot."

Tom and Sam nod and say, "OK, dad. We will be careful." They take the knife and the carrots. They try to cut them like dad. But it is hard. The carrots are tough. They have to use a lot of strength. They make funny faces and noises. They say, "This is hard work. But we can do it."

Dad watches them and laughs. He says, "You are doing great, boys. You are good helpers. I am proud of you. Soon, you will be good cooks like me." He hugs them and kisses them. He says, "I love you, Tom and Sam. You make me happy."

Tom and Sam hug him back and say, "We love you, dad. You make us happy. And you make the best food ever." They smile and keep working. They have fun in the kitchen.

Once upon a time, there were three forest animals, named Fran, Mabel, and Dandy. Fran was a rabbit, Mabel was a rabbit and Dandy was a squirrel. They all loved to gather together in the forest and play.

One day, the animals decided to have a competitive race to see who was the fasted. They all lined up at the start line and Mabel took of first. She was so fast that she didn't even see the law of the forest that said no one must run faster than the rabbits.

Before she knew it, Mabel had broken the law. Fran and Dandy were so sad. They each gathered their courage and confronted Mabel. But Mabel refused to apologize or listen.

The moral of the story is that it is important to obey and respect the law. If you don't, you might break the law and end up in trouble.
