Sam and Mia are playing in the garden. They like to run and jump and laugh. But it is very hot today. The sun is bright and the air is dry. Sam and Mia are thirsty and tired.

"Let's go inside and drink some water," Sam says to Mia. "We can play more later."

"OK," Mia says. "But we have to be alert. Mom said there are ants on the step. They can bite us if we touch them."

Sam and Mia nod. They know ants are small and fast and sometimes angry. They do not want to make them mad. They walk carefully to the door. They look at the step. They see many ants crawling on it. Some are red and some are black.

"Wow, look at all the ants!" Sam says. "They are busy. What are they doing?"

"I don't know," Mia says. "Maybe they are looking for food. Or water. Maybe they are thirsty too."

Sam and Mia feel sorry for the ants. They want to help them. They have an idea.

"Wait here," Sam says. He runs inside and gets a cup of water. He comes back and pours some water on the ground near the step. He makes a small puddle.

"Here, ants," he says. "You can drink this. It is cool and wet. It will make you happy."

Mia smiles. She thinks Sam is kind and smart. She watches the ants. Some of them stop and go to the puddle. They drink the water. They look happy.

"See, they like it!" Mia says. "You are a good friend, Sam."

Sam and Mia hug. They are happy too. They go inside and drink some water. They are not thirsty anymore. They are ready to play more. They are good friends.

Once upon a time, there were two friends named Jack and Jill. Jack wanted to be the king of the land and always told Jill that he would be the one to rule. But Jill didn't like this and refused to surrender to Jack.

One day, when Jack was playing with his cushion, Jill took it away. Jack was so angry, he started to yell at her! He said "Give me back my cushion!"

But Jill refused, throwing it from one side of the room to the other! She said "No way! I'm not going to surrender!"

Jack wasn't about to give in. He grabbed the cushion and headed for the door. But Jill was quicker and managed to get there first, standing with her feet firmly on the ground.

Jack tried pulling her away from the door, but it was no use. For the third time, he said "Give me back my cushion!"

Finally, Jill agreed to give it back, but only on one condition: that Jack agreed to share the cushion with her, using it at regular intervals. Jack agreed, and they both ended up sharing the cushion and ruling the land together.
The end.

"Shh, it's okay," Lily's mum says. "It's not real. It's just a film. The snake can't hurt you."

Lily and Tom peek at the screen. The mouse runs away from the snake. The snake slithers away. The film shows other animals again. They are happy and safe.

Lily and Tom feel better. They smile and hug each other. They watch the rest of the film. They seem to enjoy it. They clap when the film ends. They say thank you to Lily's mum. They had a good time.

Once upon a time there lived a happy little boy named Jack. He loved to play outside and make new friends.

One day, Jack was playing in the park when he stumbled upon an old, rusty trap. It was a scary sight. He froze as he tried to remember where he had seen something like it before.

Jack called out to his friend, "Hey, do you know what this is?"

His friend replied, "I think it's an animal trap. People use it to trap animals but it looks dead now."

Jack remembered hearing a story about animal traps that his grandma had told him. He shivered. He was glad he was safe from the trap's danger.

Jack and his friend decided it was best to leave the trap and never come back. They ran away as fast as they could and never looked back.

The End.

Anna and Ben were twins who liked to visit their grandma every week. Grandma lived in a big house with a nice garden and many toys. She was wealthy and gave them gifts and treats. Anna and Ben loved their grandma very much.

One day, when they went to visit her, they saw smoke coming out of her house. They were scared and ran to the door. They knocked and shouted, "Grandma, grandma, are you okay?" But no one answered. They saw a fire truck and some firefighters coming to help. They hoped grandma was safe.

The firefighters put out the fire and brought grandma out. She was coughing and had some burns. She hugged Anna and Ben and said, "I'm so glad you're here. I'm sorry, my house is ruined. I was cooking and forgot to turn off the stove. The fire started and spread quickly. I couldn't get out."

Anna and Ben felt sorry for grandma. They said, "We're sorry too, grandma. We don't care about your house or your toys or your gifts. We care about you. You're the best grandma in the world. We love you."

Grandma smiled and said, "Thank you, my darlings. You're the best twins in the world. I love you too. You know, I learned a lesson today. Having a lot of money and things doesn't make you happy. Having a loving family and friends does. I'm lucky to have you."

The moral value of the story is: Family and love are more important than money and things.

Sam and Mia like to play at the park. They like to swing, climb and slide. One day, they see a big slide that they have never tried before. It is very high and very long.

"Let's go on the big slide!" Sam says. He runs to the ladder and climbs up.

"Wait for me!" Mia says. She follows him, but she is a little scared.

They reach the top of the slide and look down. It is very steep and very fast.

"Are you ready?" Sam asks.

"I don't know," Mia says. "It looks scary."

"Don't worry, I will go first and catch you," Sam says. He is brave and wants to be a hero. He sits on the slide and pushes himself down.

"Whee!" he shouts as he slides down. He feels the wind in his hair and the sun on his face. He reaches the bottom and lands on the grass. He is happy and proud.

"Come on, Mia, it's fun!" he calls to her.

Mia looks at Sam. He is smiling and waving at her. She wants to try the slide too, but she is still scared.

"Maybe I can do it," she says to herself. She sits on the slide and holds on to the sides. She closes her eyes and slides down.

"Ahh!" she screams as she slides down. She feels the slide go up and down and twist and turn. She opens her eyes and sees the ground coming closer. She is scared and excited.

She reaches the bottom and slides off the slide. She bumps into Sam and they both fall on the grass. They are both messy and dirty, but they are also happy and laughing.

"You did it, Mia, you did it!" Sam says. He hugs her and helps her up.

"You are my hero, Sam, you are my hero!" Mia says. She hugs him back and thanks him.

Sara was sad. She missed her mom and dad. They went to work and left her with Nana. Nana was nice, but Sara wanted her mom and dad.

Nana saw Sara crying on the couch. She came over and gave her a hug. "What's wrong, Sara?" she asked.

"I want mom and dad," Sara sobbed. "They are gone for a long time."

Nana wiped Sara's tears and smiled. "They will be back soon, Sara. They love you very much. They are working hard to make money for you and them. Do you know what money is?"

Sara nodded. "Money is what you use to buy things. Like toys and clothes and food."

"That's right, Sara. And sometimes, mom and dad have to work a lot to buy those things. But they always think of you and miss you too. They will call you later and tell you how much they love you. Do you want to hear their voices?"

Sara nodded again. She liked to hear mom and dad's voices. They made her feel happy and safe.

Nana took Sara to the phone and dialed a number. She handed the phone to Sara. "Here, Sara. Say hello to mom."

Sara heard mom's voice on the phone. "Hi, Sara. How are you, my sweetie?"

"Hi, mom. I miss you," Sara said.

"I miss you too, Sara. I love you so much. Are you having fun with Nana?"

Sara looked at Nana, who smiled and winked. "Yes, mom. Nana is nice. She comforted me when I was sad. She gave me a hug and a kiss."

"That's good, Sara. Nana is very kind and caring. She loves you too. You are lucky to have her. And you know what? I have a surprise for you when I come home."

"What is it, mom?" Sara asked, curious.

"It's a secret, Sara. But I'll give you a hint. It's something yummy that you like to eat. Can you guess what it is?"

Sara thought for a moment. She liked to eat many things. But there was one thing that she liked the most. It was sweet and soft and had many colors. "Is it cake, mom?" she guessed.

Mom laughed. "You are very smart, Sara. Yes, it is cake. I bought a cake for you and dad and me. We will have a special treat tonight. How does that sound?"

Sara clapped her hands and smiled. "That sounds great, mom. I love cake. Thank you, mom."

"You're welcome, Sara. I can't wait to see you and hug you and eat cake with you. But now I have to go back to work. I'll talk to you later, okay?"

"Okay, mom. I love you. Bye."

"I love you too, Sara. Bye."

Sara hung up the phone and hugged Nana. "Mom bought a cake for us, Nana. Isn't that nice?"

"That's very nice, Sara. Mom is very thoughtful and generous. She wants to make you happy. You are lucky to have her. And she is lucky to have you. You are a good girl, Sara. You are brave and patient and polite. You make mom and dad proud."

Sara felt warm and fuzzy inside. She was happy to have Nana and mom and dad. They all loved her and she loved them. She learned that sometimes, mom and dad had to work, but they always came back. And sometimes, Nana had to comfort her, but she always made her feel better. And sometimes, they had a yummy cake, but they always shared it. They had a good rhythm of life. They were a happy family.

"What do we need to make a cake?" Lily asks.

"We need flour and eggs and milk and sugar," Ben says.

They look for the ingredients in the cupboards and the fridge. They put them in the bowl. They start to mix them with the spoon.

"Mix, mix, mix," they sing. "We are making a cake!"

But they mix too hard and too fast. The batter splashes out of the bowl. It makes a big mess on the table and the floor and their clothes.

"Oh no!" Lily says. "We are wet and sticky!"

They hear Mom coming. They are scared. They hide under the table.

"Who made this mess?" Mom says. She sees the bowl and the spoon and the batter. She sees Lily and Ben hiding under the table.

"Did you do this?" Mom asks.

Lily and Ben nod. They are sorry.

"We wanted to make a cake," Lily says.

Mom sighs. She is not happy. But she is not angry.

"Next time, you have to ask me first," Mom says. "And you have to be careful and gentle when you mix."

She helps them clean up the mess. She puts their wet clothes in the washing machine. She gives them new clothes.

She finds a cookie in her pocket. She breaks it in half. She gives one half to Lily and one half to Ben.

"Here, this is your cake for today," Mom says. "Maybe tomorrow we can make a real cake together."

Lily and Ben smile. They say thank you. They eat their cookie. They hug Mom.

They still like to play in the kitchen. But they always ask Mom first. And they always mix slowly and softly.

Toby was a careless young boy. He loved to explore the world around him. Today he decided to wear his old red jacket and explore the countryside. He skipped over the hills and ran through the fields.

He soon came across a tall oat field. He watched as the oat swayed softly in the wind. With a smile on his face he decided to explore further. He followed the oat field until he came across a small stream.

Toby found a patch of grass by the stream and sat down. He heard the sound of water running and the oat softly swaying in the wind. He felt so peaceful and content. It felt like he could stay there forever.

Suddenly he could feel something tickling his head. He looked up and saw that hundreds of oat straws had fallen on him. He had been so careless that he hadn't noticed the oat straws falling from the trees.

Toby laughed and brushed the oat straws off his head. Then he jumped up and ran back home, his red jacket billowing in the wind. He had a wonderful day and he now knew the feeling of being surrounded by nature.

Anna and Ben see a boat. The boat is red and white. It has a sail and a wheel. They want to ride the boat. They ask their moms.

"Can we ride the boat, please?" Anna says.

"Can we, can we?" Ben says.

Their moms look at the boat. They look at Anna and Ben. They nod.

"Okay, you can ride the boat. But be careful and stay close," Anna's mom says.

"Listen to the man who drives the boat. He is dependable. He knows the lake well," Ben's mom says.

Anna and Ben are happy. They run to the boat. They put on life jackets. They climb on the boat. The man who drives the boat smiles. He starts the boat. The boat moves on the lake.

Anna and Ben sit on the boat. They look at the water. They look at the sky. They see clouds and birds. They feel the wind and the sun. They are having fun.

"Look, a duck!" Anna points.

"Quack, quack!" Ben says.

They laugh. They wave to the duck. The duck swims away.

"Let's play a game," Anna says.

"What game?" Ben asks.

"Who can see more things on the lake. The one who sees more things wins," Anna says.

"Okay, let's play. I go first. I see a fish," Ben says.

"I see a flower," Anna says.

"I see a rock," Ben says.

"I see a leaf," Anna says.

They take turns. They see many things on the lake. They count them. They are both good at the game. They are both smart.

"Who wins?" Ben asks.

"I don't know. We see the same things," Anna says.

"Maybe we both win," Ben says.

"Maybe we do," Anna says.

They smile. They hug. They are both happy. They are both winners. They are both friends.

Once upon a time there was a wide river that cut through the forest. On one side of the river, a family of rabbits lived peacefully. They had plenty of food to eat and were very happy.

One day, the rabbits were out gathering food when they heard a terrible noise coming from the river. They looked over and saw a large bear struggling in the water. The bear had become stuck in the river, and was in danger of drowning. The rabbits quickly ran to help.

The rabbits tried to pull the bear out, but they were too small. They needed a plan!

Just then, one of the rabbits had an idea. "Let's get a big pill and put it in the river," said the rabbit, "We can place the pill in between the bear and the river's edge. That way, it will prevent the bear from drifting away with the current!"

The other rabbits liked the idea, so they quickly found a pill and put it in the river. Sure enough, it worked! The pill was wide and strong enough to keep the bear in place, until someone larger could come and rescue it.

The rabbits were glad that they could help, and they were also proud of their quick thinking. This story reminds us that with a bit of creativity and cooperation, even the smallest of us can make a big difference.

Once, there was a boy. He was very frustrated because he wanted to draw but he had no chalk. The boy looked around, but he couldn't find any chalk. He asked his dad for some, but his dad didn't have any either. "What should I do?" thought the boy.

Suddenly, he had an idea. He took the tiny pieces of chalk that his little sister had been using, and put them in a cup. Then he put the cup in a pot of hot water. He stirred it quickly, and after a few minutes, he poured the water out of the pot.

The boy was very surprised. Instead of tiny pieces of chalk, he found that the pieces had shrunk! Now, he had enough chalk to draw whatever he wanted.

He was so happy! He thanked his dad and quickly started to draw. He spent the whole day creating his very own masterpiece.

The boy was very proud of himself. He had used his brain and solved a problem, all by himself. He felt very proud and happy.

"I'm okay, but the bear is angry!" Sam says. He is very sorry.

The bear growls and tries to get up, but it can't. It is stuck in the trap. It is very hungry.

"Maybe we can help the bear," Mia says. She has an idea.

She runs to the bench and gets her sandwich. She throws it into the hole. The bear smells it and eats it. It is very thankful.

"Thank you, little girl," the bear says. It is very friendly.

"You're welcome, Mr. Bear," Mia says. She is very happy.

"Can you help me get out of here?" Sam asks. He is very hopeful.

"Of course, little boy," the bear says. It is very gentle.

It lifts Sam with its paw and puts him on the edge of the hole. Sam climbs out and hugs Mia. They are very relieved.

"Thank you, Mr. Bear," Sam says. He is very grateful.

"You're welcome, little boy," the bear says. It is very proud.

"Can we be your friends?" Mia asks. She is very curious.

"Sure, you can be my friends," the bear says. It is very lonely.

"Yay, we have a new friend!" Sam and Mia say. They are very excited.

They wave goodbye to the bear and run to tell their mom. They are very happy.

Once upon a time, there was a rich man who lived in a big house with his wife. He loved his wife very much and always wanted to make her happy.

One day, the rich man went to the store and bought a beautiful necklace for his wife. He knew she would love it and he couldn't wait to give it to her.

When he got home, he showed his wife the necklace and she was very happy. She put it on right away and they hugged each other.

But later that day, they went for a walk and the necklace fell off without them noticing. They searched and searched but couldn't find it anywhere. The rich man was sad because he wanted his wife to have the necklace forever.

But then, a kind stranger found the necklace and attached it to a note that said "Found this beautiful necklace, hope it brings happiness to whoever it belongs to." The rich man and his wife were so happy and grateful to the stranger for returning the necklace.

Lily decided to pray and thank God for the amazing apple. She closed her eyes and said, "Thank you, God, for this yummy apple. It's amazing!" She took a big bite and it tasted so good.

From that day on, Lily always prayed before eating her apples. She knew that God made them grow and wanted to say thank you. And every time she found an amazing apple, she knew it was a special gift from God.

Once upon a time, there was a little girl named Lily. She loved eating grapes so much that she would eat them every day. One day, she found a grape that was as big as a ball. She was so happy that she ate it all up in one bite.

But then something strange happened. Lily started to shrink! She became as small as a grape herself. She looked around and saw that everything around her was now very big. She felt scared and didn't know what to do.

Suddenly, she saw a fake flower nearby. She remembered that her mom had told her that it wasn't real. But Lily had an idea. She climbed onto the fake flower and used it to climb up to the table. From there, she was able to call out for help.

Her mom came running and saw Lily on the table. She picked her up and hugged her tightly. Lily learned that sometimes things can be big or small, real or fake, but what matters most is the love and care of those around us.

Becky had to figure out a way to get the pizza herself. She paused for a moment to think and then an idea came to her.

She walked up to the house of a wealthy man. She knocked on the door, and when he answered, she asked if he could buy her a pizza. He smiled and said, "Yes!"

Becky ran back to her house with the pizza in hand. Her mom was surprised, but pleased. She said, "Well done!"

Becky smiled. She had figured out a way to get the pizza she wanted. It was a great day!

Once upon a time there was an adorable bunny. Bunny loved to hop and bounce around the spring. Every day the little bunny would hop and bounce around like he was flying.

One day bunny was bouncing around the spring when he saw a pretty flower. The bunny stopped and said, "Oh, hello flower! You are so pretty and I love that you have many colors."

The flower replied, "Thank you! It's nice to meet you, too."

The bunny and flower then hopped around the spring together. They jumped, bounced, and had lots of fun. Soon they said goodbye, but promised they would meet again soon.

The bunny hopped back home with a big smile on his face. From then one, the bunny bounced around the spring every day, hoping to meet up with the pretty flower. He was so happy to have made a friend.

Once upon a time, there was a powerful elephant called Emma. Emma had a very big trunk and she was admired by the other animals in the forest.

One day, Emma was walking through the forest and she found a skull lying on the ground. She was curious and wanted to pick it up.

Suddenly, a voice said "Please leave the skull alone." It was a small mouse who was living in the forest.

The elephant smiled kindly and said "OK. I will leave the skull". She left it there and continued her walk through the forest.

The other animals in the forest were amazed by Emma's actions. She had shown them that it was always important to please others and to show respect.

The moral of the story is: Always be kind and consider the feelings of others before taking any action.

One day, they see a big radio on the shelf. It has many buttons and lights. They want to touch it and hear the sounds. They think Mom and Dad are not home. They climb on the chair and reach for the radio.

But they are wrong. Mom and Dad are in the kitchen. They hear a loud noise from the radio. They run to the room and see Tom and Sue with the radio. They are angry and scared.

"Tom! Sue! What are you doing?" Mom shouts. "That is our radio. It is not a toy. You could break it or hurt yourself. That is very stupid and naughty."

Tom and Sue feel bad. They drop the radio and say sorry. They hug Mom and Dad and promise not to peek at their things again. Mom and Dad forgive them and tell them to be careful and listen. They put the radio back on the shelf and take Tom and Sue to the living room. They play with their toys and books and have fun. They do not peek at the radio anymore.

Mama asked him "Do you want to pour water on the puddle?" Jonny was thrilled to do it. He filled his little pail with water from a nearby pond and started to pour it on the puddle.

When the puddle was full, he was surprised to see frogs jumping out of it. The little frogs hopped around, enjoying the cold water. Jonny was so thrilled with the sight that he kept playing with the frogs until it was time to go home.

The cat replied, "My toy is stuck in the tree. Can you help me get it?" Tom looked up and saw a red ball stuck in the tree. He wanted to help the cat, so he tried to climb the tree. As Tom climbed higher, he got close to the red ball. He reached out to grab it.

Just as Tom got the red ball, he lost his grip on the tree. He started to fall. The black cat was scared for Tom. But luckily, Tom landed on a soft pile of leaves. He was okay!

Tom gave the red ball to the black cat. The cat was very happy and thanked Tom. They became good friends and played together all day.

The man said, "I'm taking you to jail". George became more scared. He asked, "What is jail?" The man said, "It's a hot place where bad people go".

George was very scared but he didn't stop crying. He was sure he was a good boy and he didn't want to go to jail.

Just then, George's mom showed up and asked the man, "What do you think you are doing?"

The man said, "I'm just trying to help him".

George's mom said, "Thank you, but it's time for George to come home." She grabbed his hand and they both went home. George was so relieved to be home and away from that hot jail.

He asked his mom, "Mom, can I pick the rhinoceros?"

"No, Jack. That's too high for you. Maybe when you're a little older" his mom said.

Jack was disappointed but he was still excited to see the rest of the animals. While Jack was looking at the other animals, his mom ran up to him with a big surprise.

"Look, Jack! I know you wanted to pick the rhinoceros, so I found someone who is generous enough to let you do it!"

It was true! Jack was so happy that he could finally pick the rhinoceros. Using all his strength, he put both hands on it and lifted it up. What a feeling!

Jack's mom smiled at him and said, "See, Jack, I told you that if you were patient and kept your hope up, you'd get to pick the rhinoceros one day."

Mia and Leo were eager to play hide and seek in the garden. Mia counted to ten while Leo ran to find a good spot. He saw a big bush with white flowers and thought it was a perfect place to hide. He crawled under the bush and waited for Mia to find him.

Mia looked around the garden and tried to guess where Leo was. She saw the swing, the slide, the sandbox, but no Leo. She wondered if he was behind the tree or under the table. She decided to check the tree first. She walked slowly and quietly, hoping to scare Leo.

But when she reached the tree, she saw something that scared her instead. It was a big, round, white thing with green leaves. It looked like a giant cauliflower, but it had eyes and a mouth. It was a cauliflower monster!

The cauliflower monster saw Mia and opened its mouth. It said in a loud and scary voice, "Hello, little girl. Do you want to be my snack?"

Mia screamed and ran away. She was very afraid of the cauliflower monster. She wanted to find Leo and go back to the house.

Leo heard Mia scream and came out of his hiding spot. He saw the cauliflower monster and realized it was not a real monster. It was a puppet that his dad had made for a joke. He felt bad for scaring Mia. He ran after her and called her name.

"Mia, Mia, wait! It's not a real monster, it's a puppet! I'm sorry, I didn't know it was there. Please don't be mad at me!"

Mia stopped and turned around. She saw Leo holding the puppet and smiling. She realized it was a joke and felt silly for being scared. She smiled back and said, "It's okay, Leo. You didn't scare me, you just surprised me. But next time, don't hide behind a cauliflower. It's not a good spot."

The owl asked Lucy, "Do you want to learn a lesson?" Lucy nodded her head happily and the owl began to speak.

"If you're ever feeling lost, remember that wisdom will always be there for you. Just be reliable and never give up. Even if you lose something, you can always find it again if you try hard enough."

Lucy thought about the owl's words for a moment and smiled. She thanked the owl for the wise advice. From that day forward, she always kept the owl's words in mind. Whenever Lucy lost something, she remembered the owl's message and searched until she found it.

The wise owl smiled and flew away, leaving Lucy with a valuable lesson that she would never forget.

Once upon a time, there was a little girl named Lily. She loved to eat ice cream with a spoon. But one day, she accidentally dropped her favorite spoon and it broke into tiny pieces. Lily felt sad and cried a lot.

Her mother came to her and said, "Don't worry, Lily. We can get you a new spoon." Lily felt a little better but still sad.

The next day, Lily's mother surprised her with a new spoon. Lily was so happy and hugged her mother tightly. Her mother said, "See, Lily, when something bad happens, we should always hope for something good to come out of it. And now, we have a new spoon and you can enjoy your ice cream again."

From that day on, Lily learned that even when things don't go as planned, we should always hope for something good and be grateful for what we have. And whenever she used her new spoon, she remembered the lesson her mother taught her and felt quiet and content.

Lily liked to feed her dolls. She had many dolls, but her favorite was Anna. Anna had long hair and a pink dress. Lily gave Anna some water and a cookie every day.

One day, Lily saw her mom's perfume on the dresser. It smelled nice and had a pretty bottle. Lily wanted to make Anna smell nice too. She took the perfume and sprayed it on Anna's hair and dress.

But Anna did not like the perfume. It made her hair sticky and her dress wet. It also made her nose hurt. She started to cry.

Lily's mom heard the cry and came to see what was wrong. She saw Lily holding Anna and the perfume bottle.

"Lily, what did you do?" she asked.

"I wanted to feed Anna perfume, Mommy. I thought she would like it," Lily said.

"No, Lily, perfume is not for feeding. Perfume is for smelling. You can feed Anna water and cookies, but not perfume. Perfume can make her sick and ruin her clothes. Do you understand?" Mommy said.

Lily nodded. She felt sorry for Anna. She hugged her and said, "I'm sorry, Anna. I won't feed you perfume again. I love you."

Mommy smiled and said, "That's good, Lily. I love you too. Now let's go wash Anna's hair and dress. And next time, ask me before you use my perfume, okay?"

Lily agreed. She learned that perfume is not for feeding, and that she should be careful with other people's things. She also learned that Anna loved her even when she made a mistake.

Tim was a boy who liked to look at small things with his microscope. He had a microscope that his dad gave him for his birthday. He liked to look at bugs, leaves, and sand with his microscope. He learned many things from his microscope.

One day, Tim went to his friend Anna's house to play. Anna also had a microscope, but it was bigger and newer than Tim's. Anna showed Tim her microscope and said, "Look, my microscope is better than yours. It can see more things and has more lights. Do you want to try it?"

Tim felt hurt by Anna's words. He thought Anna was being mean and rude. He said, "No, I don't want to try your microscope. My microscope is good enough for me. I don't need a bigger or newer one. I like my microscope."

Anna was surprised by Tim's answer. She said, "But why? Don't you want to see more things and learn more things? Don't you want to have fun with my microscope? It's not nice to refuse a friend's offer."

Tim said, "It's not nice to make fun of a friend's gift. My dad gave me my microscope and I love it. It's special to me. You should be happy with what you have and not brag about what you have. That's not how friends behave."

Anna realized that Tim was right. She felt sorry for hurting Tim's feelings. She said, "You're right, Tim. I'm sorry for being mean and rude. I didn't mean to hurt you. I was just excited to share my microscope with you. I'm happy that you love your microscope. Can we still be friends and play with our microscopes together?"

Tim smiled and said, "Yes, we can still be friends and play with our microscopes together. Maybe we can learn from each other and see different things. Thank you for saying sorry. I'm sorry for refusing your offer. Let's have fun with our microscopes."

The moral of the story is: Be respectful of other people's feelings and belongings. Don't judge or boast about what you have or don't have. Be grateful for what you have and share it with others. Friendship is more important than things.

Once upon a time there was a nosy staff member. He worked in a store and asked a lot of questions. He was always asking people if they needed help and what they were looking for.

One day, a customer wanted to buy something and the nosy staff member asked lots of questions. The customer was getting frustrated. She wanted to be left alone.

The customer asked the nosy staff member to close the store, so she could buy something in peace. But the nosy staff member refused. He said it was against the store rules.

The customer was annoyed, so she walked away. But the nosy staff member followed her and kept asking her questions. In the end, the customer was so mad that she had to close the store herself! She was very happy when the store was finally closed and she could buy what she needed in peace.
